## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (potentially nonlinear in x), damping forces (dependent on v), and possibly external driving forces (dependent on t). The nonlinearity can appear in the spring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear spring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic spring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (combined nonlinearities)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well with hardening/softening spring behavior
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - c*x²)*v → self-excited oscillation (limit cycle) as in Van der Pol systems
- Cosine or sine functions of time → external periodic driving force; look for cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms
- Product terms x²*v or x*v → nonlinear damping that depends on amplitude, indicating energy-dependent dissipation
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with cubic velocity term → self-sustained oscillations with amplitude stabilization
- Even powers of x (x²) in restoring force → broken symmetry in the potential, leading to asymmetric oscillations
- Sine of position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like dynamics with multiple equilibria and bounded restoring force
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence of t suggests driven or parametric excitation

GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-0.19483*v + 0.19483*v*x**2 - 3.04924*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.14305*sin(v)`

The GT has these components:
1. A term proportional to `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.19483)
2. A term proportional to `v*x²` (coefficient ≈ 0.19483)
3. A term `-3.04924*x*exp(-|x|)` — this is an odd function of x
4. A term `-0.14305*sin(v)` — nonlinear in v

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)`.

**Candidate 11:** `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v + c6*v*x**2 + c7*x/(c8 + x**2) + c9*v**3`

This has `sin(c3*v + c4)`. If I set c3=1, c4=0, this gives `sin(v)`, which matches the sin(v) term. The remaining terms need to match `v`, `v*x²`, and `x*exp(-|x|)`.

The term `x*exp(-|x|)` needs to be approximated by `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c7*x/(c8 + x**2)`. These are approximations but not exact. `tanh(x)` and `x/(c+x²)` cannot exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me check if any candidate has `sin(v)` AND can exactly match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Looking through all candidates, none have `x*exp(-|x|)` explicitly. The question is whether any combination of terms can exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 50:** `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2*v + c3*v*x**2 + c4*x**3 + c5*x + c6*v**3 + c7*x*exp(c8*x)`

This has `x*exp(c8*x)`. For x > 0, `x*exp(-|x|) = x*exp(-x)`, so c8 = -1 works. But for x < 0, `x*exp(-|x|) = x*exp(x)`, so we'd need c8 = 1. Since `exp(c8*x)` can't simultaneously be `exp(-x)` for x>0 and `exp(x)` for x<0, this doesn't work exactly.

**Candidate 2:** Has `x*exp(c8*x²)`. Setting c8 < 0 gives `x*exp(-c*x²)`, which is Gaussian-like, not `x*exp(-|x|)`.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-abs(x))`. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is a very specific function that can't be exactly represented by `tanh`, rational functions, polynomials, or `x*exp(cx)` or `x*exp(cx²)`.

Also, `sin(v)` appears only implicitly in candidate 11 (via `sin(c3*v+c4)`). But even candidate 11 can't match the x-dependent part exactly.

No candidate has both the ability to exactly reproduce `sin(v)` AND `x*exp(-|x|)`. Since exact mathematical equivalence is required (for ALL values of x, v, t), approximations don't count.

Let me double-check: could `x*exp(-|x|)` be exactly zero and absorbed? No, the coefficient is -3.049, which is significant and fixed.

None of the candidates can exactly reproduce the GT for all values of the variables.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO38)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-0.194830767863936*v + 0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v` (linear in v)
2. `v*x²` 
3. `x*exp(-|x|)` (odd function of x)
4. `sin(v)` (odd function of v)

Key observations:
- `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function of x that decays exponentially
- `sin(v)` is a nonlinear function of v
- No polynomial terms in x alone, no x² terms, no v³ terms, no t dependence

Now let me analyze the candidates. The critical question for each is whether its basis functions can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)`.

**For `x*exp(-|x|)`:** This is NOT a rational function, NOT `tanh(x)`, NOT a polynomial, NOT `x/(c+x²)`. However, `tanh(x)` is an odd sigmoid-like function, and `x*exp(-|x|)` is also odd and bell-shaped. They are NOT the same function. Similarly, `x/(c+x²)` is a Lorentzian-like function - also not the same.

Can any combination of the candidate basis functions exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`? Let me check if `tanh(cx) + x/(d+x²)` could equal `x*exp(-|x|)` - these are all odd functions of x, but they have different functional forms. `tanh` approaches ±1 asymptotically while `x*exp(-|x|)` approaches 0. Adding `x/(d+x²)` (which also approaches 0) could help, but `tanh(cx)` still approaches ±1. So we'd need the tanh coefficient to be 0, leaving just `x/(d+x²)`, which decays as 1/x, not exponentially. These are fundamentally different.

**For `sin(v)`:** This requires a sinusoidal function of v. Only candidates with `sin(v)` or equivalent can match.

Let me check each candidate systematically:

- **Candidates with `sin(v)`:** Only Candidate 11 has `sin(c3*v + c4)`, which can represent `sin(v)` with c3=1, c4=0.
- **Candidates with `sin(x+c)` or `sin(t+c)`:** Candidates 8, 10, 17, 19 have sin of x or t, not v.

For Candidate 11: `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v + c6*v*x² + c7*x/(c8 + x²) + c9*v³`

This has `sin(v)` ✓, `v` ✓, `v*x²` ✓, but for the x-dependent part it has `tanh(c1*x) + x/(c8+x²)`. Can this combination equal `x*exp(-|x|)`? As argued above, no - `tanh` approaches constants at infinity while `x*exp(-|x|)` decays to 0. Even with `x/(c8+x²)` added, the tanh term dominates at large |x|. Setting c0=0 leaves only `x/(c8+x²)` which decays as 1/x, not exponentially. And there's a `v³` term that can be zeroed.

So even Candidate 11 cannot match because `x/(c+x²)` ≠ `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by any combination of `tanh(x)`, `x/(c+x²)`, polynomials in x, or `x*exp(cx²)` (Gaussian decay ≠ exponential decay), and `sin(v)` cannot be represented by `v³`, `log(v²+1)`, `exp(v²)`, or other non-sinusoidal v-functions, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify: None of the candidates contain both `x*exp(-|x|)` (or equivalent) AND `sin(v)`.
